<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17530973760257291412"><div>Nestled in the heart of the Adirondacks, Miller's Kill, New York is about as safe as it gets. That's why Episcopal minister Clare Fergusson is shocked when the July Fourth weekend brings a rash of vicious assaults to the scenic town. Even Clare's good friend, police chief Russ Van Alstyne, is shaken by the brutality of the crimes-especially when it appears that the victims</div></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17530973760257291412"><div>Nestled in the heart of the Adirondacks, Miller's Kill, New York is about as safe as it gets. That's why Episcopal minister Clare Fergusson is shocked when the July Fourth weekend brings a rash of vicious assaults to the scenic town. Even Clare's good friend, police chief Russ Van Alstyne, is shaken by the brutality of the crimes-especially when it appears that the victims were chosen because they are gay. But when a third assault of an out-of-town developer ends in murder, Clare and Russ wonder if the recent crime wave is connected to the victim's controversial plan to open an upscale spa in Miller's Kill. But not all things in the tiny town are what they seem-and soon, Clare and Russ are left to fight their unspoken attraction to one another even as they uncover a labyrinthine conspiracy that threatens to turn deadly for them both...<br />
</div></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17530973760257291412">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_5994766">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5994766" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/250195-lj" class="left imgcol" title="LJ"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1436467895p2/250195.jpg" alt="LJ" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/5994766?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 10, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/250195-lj" class="user" title="LJ">LJ</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1260935.A_Fountain_Filled_With_Blood" title="Hardcover 9780312304102" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=amateur_sleuth" class="actionLinkLite">amateur_sleuth</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=contemporary_post_1945" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary_post_1945</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=new_york_state" class="actionLinkLite">new_york_state</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer5994766">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1448086212801021795">Two gay men are brutally attacked in Spencer-Fleming's second Reverend Clare Fergusson mystery. Clare, a former army helicopter pilot, now a priest at St. Alban's Episcopal Church in the small Adirondack town of Millers Kill, New York, feels the attacks are related, and the police should notify the community so people can protect themselves. Police Chief Russ Van Alstyne disagrees, wanting to avoid copycat crimes, and his refusal to act creates tension between the two, further complicated by the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1448086212801021795">Two gay men are brutally attacked in Spencer-Fleming's second Reverend Clare Fergusson mystery. Clare, a former army helicopter pilot, now a priest at St. Alban's Episcopal Church in the small Adirondack town of Millers Kill, New York, feels the attacks are related, and the police should notify the community so people can protect themselves. Police Chief Russ Van Alstyne disagrees, wanting to avoid copycat crimes, and his refusal to act creates tension between the two, further complicated by their mutual attraction, although Russ is married. When a third man is killed, Clare launches her own investigation. Serious issues such as gay bashing and contamination of the town's water supply with PCBs add depth to the story.<br /><br />Please remember, this is my opinion only. I finally figured out what so bothered me about this series—it’s the character Clare. This is a woman who was an Army pilot, with all the rules, chain-of-command, “need to know, ” and discipline associated therewith, and is now an Episcopal priest, with all its associated confidentiality, discipline and rules. And yet, she blathers information she was expressly asked not to, she is attracted to a married man when part of her job is providing counseling for couples, and interferes in a police investigation. Not to mention she now drive a Shelby Cobra which, if not a replica, is approximately a $50,000 vehicle. <br /><br />Interestingly, had the author made the protagonist a lawyer, which was her profession, I don’t think any of these things would have bothered me. I guess it shows the different ethic I hold for ministers and lawyers. I think the police chief is very well done and realistic, and were he the sole focus of the series, I would like it. However, Clare just does not ring true to me. So, I fear, this is not a series with which I personally shall continue.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1448086212801021795">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_25378398">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/25378398" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/98395-red" class="left imgcol" title="Red"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1189784525p2/98395.jpg" alt="Red" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/25378398?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 30, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/98395-red" class="user" title="Red">Red</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/98395-red?shelf=kindle-books" class="actionLinkLite">kindle-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/98395-red?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer25378398">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4786850326525638809">I really like these books. They have a nice strong female character. It's interesting and novel that Clare is an Episcopalian priest, who used to be an Army helicopter pilot. I like the setting, a small town in upstate New York. Her best friend and forbidden romantic interest, is the already married police chief. This presents a quandary for me, because even though you'd like characters to get together, I'm not the least bit keen about the breaking up of his marriage. I assume that somewhere fur</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4786850326525638809">I really like these books. They have a nice strong female character. It's interesting and novel that Clare is an Episcopalian priest, who used to be an Army helicopter pilot. I like the setting, a small town in upstate New York. Her best friend and forbidden romantic interest, is the already married police chief. This presents a quandary for me, because even though you'd like characters to get together, I'm not the least bit keen about the breaking up of his marriage. I assume that somewhere further along in the series, that probably happens.<br /><br />The mysteries are interesting, and she throws out enough red herrings that guessing 'who done it' will keep you guessing. Although, I'm worried about the trap that TV shows fall into, the biggest named guest star is usually the killer. In this series, unless she has mysteries other than murder, one has to wonder, how many murderers can live in one small town. So that leaves you to suspect the out-of-towners in the stories, a much smaller pool to draw from.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4786850326525638809">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/1145657-hallie" class="user" title="Hallie">Hallie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer846951307">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4083509548494312881">As I pretty much finished this, slept, did the things I *had* to do (on a Saturday, with a bad headache and the ability to let myself off the hook for a lot of things I probably *should* have done) and launched straight into book 3, I'm both a bit fuzzy about what happened where and pretty clearly addicted to this series. But whether this is a healthy addiction that will do no harm at all, ever, to anyone, or whether it'll break my heart, ruin my family, bring shame and ... All right, enough hyp</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4083509548494312881">As I pretty much finished this, slept, did the things I *had* to do (on a Saturday, with a bad headache and the ability to let myself off the hook for a lot of things I probably *should* have done) and launched straight into book 3, I'm both a bit fuzzy about what happened where and pretty clearly addicted to this series. But whether this is a healthy addiction that will do no harm at all, ever, to anyone, or whether it'll break my heart, ruin my family, bring shame and ... All right, enough hyperbole!<br /><br />The mystery in this book wasn't that strong, so all the weight fell on the characters and setting, but for the most part, the mystery is a bit frosting anyway. I continue to love Clare and Russ, and am surprised at how much I'm loving a Forbidden Love story. So not my cup of tea normally, but their mutual care and their very different and also utterly the same senses of honour just makes it perfect. What made me almost weepy in this book was what happens when Clare does something she really shouldn't, and does it on a full tank of self-righteousness, which leads her to hurt Russ after making him angry. She's very unfair and acknowledges it freely, but Russ is able to move beyond the hurt and make an admission of his own, one he knows she won't like but that he can trust her to help him with, instead of rejecting him. <br /><br />That ending, too - no wonder I could barely resist grabbing the next book immediately. Also: <em>Linda's not a pet person.</em> What more needs to be said?</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4083509548494312881">...more</a>

        rated it

            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer893795349">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17842977244168229564">I'm still very engaged with the whole relationship between Russ and Clare and how they deal with their mutual attraction. I'm also still amused/fascinated by Russ's wife Linda's non-appearance; it's impressive that she can exert such a control on the story simply by existing. Russ's mother amused me tremendously, mostly because of how different she is from her son, but also because she's as committed to her beliefs as Clare is. I'm definitely finding that the characters rather than the mysteries</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17842977244168229564">I'm still very engaged with the whole relationship between Russ and Clare and how they deal with their mutual attraction. I'm also still amused/fascinated by Russ's wife Linda's non-appearance; it's impressive that she can exert such a control on the story simply by existing. Russ's mother amused me tremendously, mostly because of how different she is from her son, but also because she's as committed to her beliefs as Clare is. I'm definitely finding that the characters rather than the mysteries are what are keeping me connected to the series. In this case, I figured out the true villain before Russ and Clare did, though not the surprise extra villain at the end, but that didn't bother me much because of the way the story ends up being more thriller than mystery. Spencer-Fleming has such a good handle on description and characterization that I find myself forgiving her any weaknesses in plot. I'm really looking forward to seeing what happens with Clare and her new boyfriend; she thinks it will help her get over these feelings for Russ, but I, as omniscient reader, know that she is kidding herself.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17842977244168229564">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16164763787462781404">From one temperature extreme to the other! Wow, this book was good and kept up the same high standard for the sophomore book in the series. What I especially enjoy about Julia Spencer-Fleming is her characterization. Clare and Russ (and all the other bit part players) are 3-dimensional and real. I like and respect them, I care when they are in danger, I worry about their choices...I'm invested!<br /><br />As a constant reader always searching for new books, what really 'draws me in' is characterization as s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16164763787462781404">From one temperature extreme to the other! Wow, this book was good and kept up the same high standard for the sophomore book in the series. What I especially enjoy about Julia Spencer-Fleming is her characterization. Clare and Russ (and all the other bit part players) are 3-dimensional and real. I like and respect them, I care when they are in danger, I worry about their choices...I'm invested!<br /><br />As a constant reader always searching for new books, what really 'draws me in' is characterization as strong and as vivid as in this series. I see by JS-F's Goodreads profile that she counts Lois McMaster-Bujold and Margaret Maron as favorites/influences--two of my favorite authors and both known for exceptional characterization themselves. That explains a lot as to why these are such good books, I think. I always like to see what authors count as influences and what they read themselves. Being able to recognize and be influenced by the best leads to producing more of the best, I think.<br /><br />Some of my best recommendations have come from seeing why my favorite authors recommend or have read themselves.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/971945-kathy?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/971945-kathy?shelf=highly-recommend" class="actionLinkLite">highly-recommend</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/971945-kathy?shelf=series" class="actionLinkLite">series</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/971945-kathy?shelf=favorite-authors" class="actionLinkLite">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/971945-kathy?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer649843481">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1907826292346617235">In the second novel of the Clare Fergusson/Russ Van Alstyne series, the priest and the police chief must confront crimes of hate in their small idyllic Adirondack town. Homophobia has reared its ugly head, and Clare once again has her heart and head in involved in both discovering its source and bringing it to the attention of her Episcopalian church and the community. Russ, while equally appalled by these crimes, is more focused on catching the perpetrators of first two assaults and then a murd</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1907826292346617235">In the second novel of the Clare Fergusson/Russ Van Alstyne series, the priest and the police chief must confront crimes of hate in their small idyllic Adirondack town. Homophobia has reared its ugly head, and Clare once again has her heart and head in involved in both discovering its source and bringing it to the attention of her Episcopalian church and the community. Russ, while equally appalled by these crimes, is more focused on catching the perpetrators of first two assaults and then a murder than he is on educating the masses. Of course, Clare is quite capable of doing two impossible tasks at once. This book also continues the struggle that Clare and Russ have in resisting their attraction to one another, testing Clare's convictions and Russ's marriage vows. Clare meets Mrs. Van Alstyne in this story, but it is the mother of Russ, not his wife, and the two women hit it off, as might be expected. <br /><br />Julia Spencer-Fleming has quickly become one of my favorite mystery/crime authors. Her mastery at writing action scenes, and there are several, is electrifying. I found myself reading these scenes as fast as I could to keep up with the excitement of the moment contained within them. Just outstanding! Again, Spencer-Fleming's powers of description are hypnotic. You are in that setting; you are in that character. No time to linger on this review, as #3 in the series is waiting for me. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1907826292346617235">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer122730673">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8095904376192012391">The Big Bopper lyrics for Chantilly Lace keep going through my head when I think about my feelings for Fountain Filled with Blood. "You Know What I Like". <br /><br />There's something comforting about reading a series and spending time with characters that you get to know and love. And love I do Episcopalian Priest Clare Ferguson, Police Chief Russ Van Alstyne and the other inhabitants of Millers Kill, a fictitious town somewhere in the Adirondacks, NY. <br /><br /><br />The mysteries are light, the killing doesn't gross me</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8095904376192012391">The Big Bopper lyrics for Chantilly Lace keep going through my head when I think about my feelings for Fountain Filled with Blood. "You Know What I Like". <br /><br />There's something comforting about reading a series and spending time with characters that you get to know and love. And love I do Episcopalian Priest Clare Ferguson, Police Chief Russ Van Alstyne and the other inhabitants of Millers Kill, a fictitious town somewhere in the Adirondacks, NY. <br /><br /><br />The mysteries are light, the killing doesn't gross me out, a good read for a winter's day. The romantic tension between Clare and married Russ, tickles me. <br /><br />I've read only 3 in the series, one out of order and have enjoyed them all. I like the cliff hanger approach at the end of one to entice me to read the next. <br /><br />There are rumors that the seventh, One was a Soldier, may be the last. I'm usually in favor of ending series before they become stale but in this case I could go a few more. <br /><br />When will Goodreads allow that .5 star? 3.5 stars for this one. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_67863806">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/67863806" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/175709-abby" class="left imgcol" title="Abby"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1377193647p2/175709.jpg" alt="Abby" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/67863806?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 25, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/175709-abby" class="user" title="Abby">Abby</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/175709-abby?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer67863806">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11195995839419024525">I stayed up waaaaay too late reading this one, even though I pretty much had the mystery all figured out. What kept me up so late at night was the continuing dynamic between Reverend Clare Fergusson and the married Chief of Police, Russ Van Alstyne. After spending the remaining winter and spring studiously avoiding each other, they are together again, determined to keep attraction at bay, and figure out who's behind a series of vicious hate crimes in small town Miller's Kill, NY.<br /><br />The mystery wasn</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11195995839419024525">I stayed up waaaaay too late reading this one, even though I pretty much had the mystery all figured out. What kept me up so late at night was the continuing dynamic between Reverend Clare Fergusson and the married Chief of Police, Russ Van Alstyne. After spending the remaining winter and spring studiously avoiding each other, they are together again, determined to keep attraction at bay, and figure out who's behind a series of vicious hate crimes in small town Miller's Kill, NY.<br /><br />The mystery wasn't a taut as the previous and more than a little messy in some parts, and the helicopter scene was just way over the top. But Spencer-Fleming maintains slow burn, tension and intensity of not only the investigation but between Clare and Russ. There's a scene that made me laugh out loud when Clare and Russ are bantering about the use of the a/c in his truck. It was pitch perfect to the same 'argument' Ed and I have about a/c in his car, too.<br /><br />That's what I love about these books. They are, indeed, "pitch perfect". The dialogue, characterization, motivations, scenery -- I can see, hear, feel and smell it all.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11195995839419024525">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_27016285">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27016285" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/113980-trin" class="left imgcol" title="Trin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1181029461p2/113980.jpg" alt="Trin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/27016285?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 18, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/113980-trin" class="user" title="Trin">Trin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/113980-trin?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/113980-trin?shelf=american-lit" class="actionLinkLite">american-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer27016285">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9446152142128659019">Sequel to <a title=" In the Bleak Midwinter" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20In%20the%20Bleak%20Midwinter"> In the Bleak Midwinter</a>. I loved the first three-fourths of this, though I think it kind of fell apart at the end. Among the good: meeting Russ’ wonderfully eccentric mom, Clare helping Russ confront his internalized homophobia (and his willingness to do so, which shows, despite his discomfort, what a good man he is), Clare interrupting her investigations to get drunk and flirty with a cute Brit—a sequence that, since it’s her, ends with her jumping out a second story window. It’s nice</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9446152142128659019">Sequel to <a title=" In the Bleak Midwinter" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20In%20the%20Bleak%20Midwinter"> In the Bleak Midwinter</a>. I loved the first three-fourths of this, though I think it kind of fell apart at the end. Among the good: meeting Russ’ wonderfully eccentric mom, Clare helping Russ confront his internalized homophobia (and his willingness to do so, which shows, despite his discomfort, what a good man he is), Clare interrupting her investigations to get drunk and flirty with a cute Brit—a sequence that, since it’s her, ends with her jumping out a second story window. It’s nice, in a sophomore effort, to feel like you’re really getting comfortable with the characters, and this book also has a mystery that honestly did keep me anxiously on the edge of my seat.<br /><br />However, I felt everything that led up to getting Clare in the pilot’s seat of that helicopter seemed rather contrived. I understand why Spencer-Fleming wanted to go there, but I don’t think she quite made it work. And following on the helicopter sequence’s heels, the unraveling of the conspiracy at the end felt unsuspenseful and almost airless.<br /><br />In general, I just don’t think my enjoyment of this book could match my delight at the discovery of the first, but I’m still looking forward to the next one and seeing Russ and Clare’s relationship progress.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9446152142128659019">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14925812664616936252">I find these books JUST good enough to keep reading - nice, easy-to-read mysteries that draw me in enough to want to know who done it. The first one in the series was better, less predictable. I may read the third after I read a number of other books on my list. (not sure)<br /><br />My biggest problem with the book: the characters. First, I don't get the attraction between Russ and Clare. I don't feel it. I don't buy it. I'm TOLD it is there. Reminds me of high school English class when the teacher said, "</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14925812664616936252">I find these books JUST good enough to keep reading - nice, easy-to-read mysteries that draw me in enough to want to know who done it. The first one in the series was better, less predictable. I may read the third after I read a number of other books on my list. (not sure)<br /><br />My biggest problem with the book: the characters. First, I don't get the attraction between Russ and Clare. I don't feel it. I don't buy it. I'm TOLD it is there. Reminds me of high school English class when the teacher said, "show, not tell" in your writing. It seems forced, disingenuous. And the forbidden love aspect is over-the-top. He's the married chief of police in a small town. She's a priest. I'm surprised the author didn't name them Capulet and Montague. <br /><br />Secondly, Clare is so annoying. She constantly butts in where it's none of her business, tells the police how to do their job, puts herself in danger while conducting her own "investigations," etc. If she were a teenager, she might be a likable, spunky heroine, but she is in her mid-30s, should know better, and just comes off as annoying. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15049377005390266539">Hey, I liked this one too!<br /><br />And the thing I liked, most particularly (still not the mystery) is how this relationship is between two <em>really</em> different people. The most obvious way is in their politics – she’s a bleeding heart liberal, he’s a head-in-the-sand social conservative in the way some people are by virtue of pretending that a lot of problems aren’t problems. And they argue about this stuff! Like grownups! In ways that make neither of them look stupid in the long term! That is so refreshing</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15049377005390266539">Hey, I liked this one too!<br /><br />And the thing I liked, most particularly (still not the mystery) is how this relationship is between two <em>really</em> different people. The most obvious way is in their politics – she’s a bleeding heart liberal, he’s a head-in-the-sand social conservative in the way some people are by virtue of pretending that a lot of problems aren’t problems. And they argue about this stuff! Like grownups! In ways that make neither of them look stupid in the long term! That is so refreshing. I had no idea how tired I was of the sameness of romantic relationships – we love each other because we think the same way about everything important.<br /><br />(Although points off for trotting out one of the more damaging liberal clichés: the “I know you’re not a homophobe because you care enough to worry about the question.” Uh, no. That’s what we call self-congratulatory crap. Knowing enough to ask the question is not an inoculation against being a homophobe/racist/whatever, because the isms are systemic and subconscious. “You can’t be a homophobe, you’re worried about being a homophobe,” is a correlate to the lovely thought that brought us hipster racism. And it does not belong in this otherwise thoughtful, deeply humane book.)<br /></span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10875480662624108913">I feel like I'm not going to know what I think about this series until I read more! (Well, I'm enjoying it.) (This isn't too much of a spoiler.) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[I'm fascinated that Russ's wife has no physical presence in the series (that I've read). At times, I've wondered if that's taking the easy way out, but I don't think that's exactly true. Because her presence is felt. But it's so . . . I get the feeling that if she didn't exist, Russ and Clare would already be solidly together. But she does exist and they both honor that. And that's just so . . . to see that, these two people who fit so well together, but can't be together for good reasons (when Clare was commenting about how marriage should be forever), it's just . . . a really interesting situation. I don't even know if I can see I ship them. I JUST LIKE THEM A LOT. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Big spoilers. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[Okay, but the first book's villain killed himself! No fair using the same plot device her. I also suspected Peggy was up to something with the water bottles and was pretty sure she was when she told them to fly the guy straight to the hospital. DON'T BELIEVE THAT. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Oh, and be careful if you're reading the Kindle edition. Mine had formatting issues here and there, including several paragraphs out of place in the climax scene, oops!<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_99308984">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99308984" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2220862-joyce-lagow" class="left imgcol" title="Joyce Lagow"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1389851374p2/2220862.jpg" alt="Joyce Lagow" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/99308984?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 20, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2220862-joyce-lagow" class="user" title="Joyce Lagow">Joyce Lagow</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1260935.A_Fountain_Filled_With_Blood" title="Hardcover 9780312304102" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer99308984">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14945252789591856174">2nd in the Reverend Clare Fergusson/Russ Van Alstyne series.[return][return]A well-respected medical examiner, who is gay, is beaten to within an inch of his life. Shocked by the appearance of such a hate crime, Clare urges Rush to warn other gays in Miller s Kill about the incident. Russ refuses, afraid that that will merely incite copycat crimes. Within a short time, yet another gay man is severely beaten in his video rental store, ratcheting the tension between Clare and Russ higher.[return][</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14945252789591856174">2nd in the Reverend Clare Fergusson/Russ Van Alstyne series.[return][return]A well-respected medical examiner, who is gay, is beaten to within an inch of his life. Shocked by the appearance of such a hate crime, Clare urges Rush to warn other gays in Miller s Kill about the incident. Russ refuses, afraid that that will merely incite copycat crimes. Within a short time, yet another gay man is severely beaten in his video rental store, ratcheting the tension between Clare and Russ higher.[return][return]Meanwhile, Russ s feisty 69 year old mother is leading a protest against a resort development just outside of Miller s Kill that may be releasing PCBs from an old storage site into the waters and ground of the town. As it happens, one of the partners in the development company is a gay man. During a 4th of July fireworks celebration, Clare stumbles across his body in a park. [return][return]Environmental issues and hate crimes are twin matrices in Spencer-Fleming s second novel in this excellent series. When done well, themes such as these can add a great deal to the interest of a plot. While both are necessary for the plot, Spencer-Fleming does not handle these themes that well, especially the environmental one. It feels forced; her description of the major demonstration is even faintly ridiculous. The hate crime theme is more neutral but other than to serve as a mask in the plot, does not do much for the story.[return][return]Spencer-Fleming s writing is not that outstanding, but served her well in her first novel. In this the second, it is distinctly more mediocre. The verb  to snort is overused, not to say abused; you really can t use it twice in the same paragraph and hope to get a good effect.[return][return]The climax of the book includes a helicopter crash which should be gripping but falls short because I, for one, don t know the terminology of helicopter anatomy well enough to be able to follow what happens after the crash. I had to take it on faith that it was a tense time where the situation could have deteriorated badly. It was really too bad.[return][return]The plot is good but not anything out of the ordinary. It serves.[return][return]But, Spencer-Fleming s strengths are present as well. Her sense of humor, on display through her characters reactions to situations, especially that of Clare, is wry and at times wonderfully self-deprecating as well. Russ and Clare are strong characters with distinct and believable personalities. The setting, in northeast New York State, is well done; clearly Spencer-Fleming knows her small towns and the geography of the area.[return][return]I found the book a letdown after the excellent debut novel,<em> In The Bleak Midwinter</em>. Still, though something of a disappointment, Spencer-Fleming endowed her characters and situation well enough to keep interest in the series going.[return][return]</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14945252789591856174">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer186585901">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11493687360056258674">Another mystery I liked better than I thought I would. The crime solver in this series is a former Army pilot, turned Episcopal priest in upstate New York. Obviously the way she gets involved in solving the crime is a bit contrived, but otherwise the genre just doesn't work! I am enjoying the building tension between her and the police chief, although I struggle with whether he is a schlumpy, small town cop with a unsympathetic wife, 16 years her senior, or if he's a almost fit, handsome, former</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11493687360056258674">Another mystery I liked better than I thought I would. The crime solver in this series is a former Army pilot, turned Episcopal priest in upstate New York. Obviously the way she gets involved in solving the crime is a bit contrived, but otherwise the genre just doesn't work! I am enjoying the building tension between her and the police chief, although I struggle with whether he is a schlumpy, small town cop with a unsympathetic wife, 16 years her senior, or if he's a almost fit, handsome, former stud with an unsympathetic wide. Also the bits where each person says "excuse my French" when pretending not to swear in front of others is overused and stupid. People in real life either swear in front of people they know or they refrain. I can understand no one wanting to swear in front a priest, but once she swears in front of you or you rescue her in some way, or you've traipsed all over and shared "moments', its time to stop pretending to be overly polite. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6773468755122719715">This was just as good as the first book (In the Bleak Midwinter) I highly recommend this series as Clare is a very interesting character and the mysteries are well drawn. She is a former Army Air Force Captain and helicopter pilot, the change from flying missions in the Gulf War to being the Episcopal priest of a small town NY State parish means sometimes we glimpse the adrenaline junkie Clare who jumps in with both feet (literally sometimes) The plot of AFFWB is quite topical to current events</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6773468755122719715">This was just as good as the first book (In the Bleak Midwinter) I highly recommend this series as Clare is a very interesting character and the mysteries are well drawn. She is a former Army Air Force Captain and helicopter pilot, the change from flying missions in the Gulf War to being the Episcopal priest of a small town NY State parish means sometimes we glimpse the adrenaline junkie Clare who jumps in with both feet (literally sometimes) The plot of AFFWB is quite topical to current events as the story begins with an attack on a gay man leaving a dinner with friends which causes quite a stir in the small town of Miller's Kill. Clare does manage to do some pretty reckless things, her ability to stand back and observe rather than act rarely occurs, instead, she is in the thick of the investigation even though it places a strain on her to be in proximity of the (married) police chief, Russ Van Alstyne who has proven to be a kindred spirit.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5945479205071748539">This sequel fleshed out much more of the back-story of the protagonists, anchoring their personalities within their own histories. <br /><br />The inevitability of Clare's love of helicopters and Russ's phobia of flying in them was established early in the first novel. <span id="freeTextContainer2507285258250470042">There certainly was plenty of blood in this book! But the heroine of it totally turned me off. She is an Episcopal preist who seemed to me to violate every tenet of her profession, getting into all sorts of scrapes necessitating her rescue by the chief of police who is trying to solve a number of brutal murders which she thinks are tied to gay-bashing in the community, and which she feels something should be done about, although the police chief thinks otherwise. In addition, she was a helicopte</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2507285258250470042">There certainly was plenty of blood in this book! But the heroine of it totally turned me off. She is an Episcopal preist who seemed to me to violate every tenet of her profession, getting into all sorts of scrapes necessitating her rescue by the chief of police who is trying to solve a number of brutal murders which she thinks are tied to gay-bashing in the community, and which she feels something should be done about, although the police chief thinks otherwise. In addition, she was a helicopter pilot in the first Gulf War and the adventures surrounding this circumstance, including a helicopter crash while trying to rescue another possible murder victim, seem totally improbable. In real life they would all have instantly been killed. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1447382779">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1447382779" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6535930-pamela-shropshire" class="left imgcol" title="Pamela Shropshire"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1420326873p2/6535930.jpg" alt="Pamela Shropshire" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1447382779?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 20, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6535930-pamela-shropshire" class="user" title="Pamela Shropshire">Pamela Shropshire</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1447382779">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3032790761074952827">After I finished In the Bleak Midwinter, I immediately downloaded this book. I simply could not resist learning more about Clare and Russ.<br /><br />Clare is such an intriguing character. In some ways, she is very conservative. She was an Army officer and flew helicopters. She is now an Episcopal priest who is, as she put it, "practicing celibacy." Her daily routine is fairly rigid - she is a dedicated runner who runs every morning without fail.<br /><br />And yet in other areas, she is extremely liberal and feminist.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3032790761074952827">After I finished In the Bleak Midwinter, I immediately downloaded this book. I simply could not resist learning more about Clare and Russ.<br /><br />Clare is such an intriguing character. In some ways, she is very conservative. She was an Army officer and flew helicopters. She is now an Episcopal priest who is, as she put it, "practicing celibacy." Her daily routine is fairly rigid - she is a dedicated runner who runs every morning without fail.<br /><br />And yet in other areas, she is extremely liberal and feminist. This side of her dominates in this book, in which gays are being targeted and severely beaten. She only half jokingly tells Russ that she intends to organize a Gay Pride parade.<br /><br />Speaking of Russ. His character is further developed in this book as well. He professes to be an atheist, yet attends a number if services at St. Alban's and even prays at one point (when the helicopter he and Clare are in begins to crash, which puts one in mind of the old saying "there are no atheists in foxholes). <br /><br />We also meet Russ's mother and what a surprise she is! She is, as Russ describes her, "old lefty peacenik." It's very funny when Russ has to arrest her for an unlicensed protest/demonstration!<br /><br />I seem to have focused completely on the characters to the exclusion of the murder/plot. But this is appropriate, since it is primarily the characters that are so enjoyable.<br /><br />Russ and Clare are very strongly attracted to each other. But of course he is married (although his wife seems quite distant and even cold towards Russ) and Clare, being a religious, takes the sin of adultery quite seriously. In one poignant moment between the two, Clare asks Russ what he's thinking about and he replies "Jimmy Carter." Clare recognizes the reference (when the President said that he had committed adultery in his heart many times).<br /><br />Clare meets a charming Englishman, Hugh Pargeter, at a party where they trade witty banter and double entendres. Later, she brings Hugh as her date to a dinner party where Russ is also a guest (he brings his mother). Clare tells Russ she decided she needed to start dating and it didn't really matter who.<br /><br />I've already downloaded the next book in the series.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3032790761074952827">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1131097473">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1131097473" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3985398-sara-cat" class="left imgcol" title="Sara Cat"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1327286105p2/3985398.jpg" alt="Sara Cat" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1131097473?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 13, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3985398-sara-cat" class="user" title="Sara Cat">Sara Cat</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3985398-sara-cat?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1131097473">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17925137728369381613">So hard to rank these. 3.5 stars. They just leave you wanting a little more of everything - character depth, a look at the life of a priest, backstory, villany, etc. Everything runs a little flat.<br /><br />The premise is so good, and she writes a great action climax that in this and the last book made a lot of the other stuff worth the slog. This book was better than the last and looking at reviews, it seems like they keep getting better. Yet, for some reason, the essence of the mysteries seem to me to be</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17925137728369381613">So hard to rank these. 3.5 stars. They just leave you wanting a little more of everything - character depth, a look at the life of a priest, backstory, villany, etc. Everything runs a little flat.<br /><br />The premise is so good, and she writes a great action climax that in this and the last book made a lot of the other stuff worth the slog. This book was better than the last and looking at reviews, it seems like they keep getting better. Yet, for some reason, the essence of the mysteries seem to me to be forced, as does the attraction between the two leads. Setting (Adirondacks), which is also an important part of mystery series (who would Lucas Davenport be not in Minnesota?) has a lot of potential, but not fully developed. Main attraction is Reverend Clare's character. They are fine for filler reading, but I have the feeling she could be so much better! A little more depth, a little less exposition, a little bit more fullness to the characters...I will end up going back to read the next one and see how things go.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17925137728369381613">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1103421965">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1103421965" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/22642807-marta" class="left imgcol" title="Marta"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Marta" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1103421965?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 11, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/22642807-marta" class="user" title="Marta">Marta</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1103421965">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12476829307448621426">The second mystery in the series about Reverend Clare Fergusson, a former Army helicopter pilot, now an Episcopal priest in upstate New York. I like the snippets of Episcopal services and prayers that appear in the story, so familiar from growing up. Clare’s friendship with Sheriff Russ deepens in this one throughout, but especially during the desperate helicopter rescue flight, crash, and hike out toward the end, when Russ’ worst experiences in Vietnam and their lasting effects are revealed. Cl</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12476829307448621426">The second mystery in the series about Reverend Clare Fergusson, a former Army helicopter pilot, now an Episcopal priest in upstate New York. I like the snippets of Episcopal services and prayers that appear in the story, so familiar from growing up. Clare’s friendship with Sheriff Russ deepens in this one throughout, but especially during the desperate helicopter rescue flight, crash, and hike out toward the end, when Russ’ worst experiences in Vietnam and their lasting effects are revealed. Clare and Russ have acknowledged their attraction in this book, are fighting it, and becoming aware that other people see it, too. The story takes place in mid-summer this time and I enjoyed the descriptions of the woods and even sailing on the lake. The initial theme is gay bashing and, although it ultimately came down to money and greed, it was interesting to see Clare work with her vestry in a debate about the position and action her church should take. When they came up with a candlelight vigil I thought, of course! Clare is invited to perform a gay marriage at the end for her good friends and has to weigh her personal convictions against knowing what her church and its government will want her to do. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12476829307448621426">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1014142928">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1014142928" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/9919989-olivermagnus" class="left imgcol" title=" Olivermagnus  "><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1406988553p2/9919989.jpg" alt=" Olivermagnus  " /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1014142928?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 02, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/9919989-olivermagnus" class="user" title=" Olivermagnus  "> Olivermagnus  </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/9919989-olivermagnus?shelf=contemporary-mystery" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1014142928">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12415484227144343717">It's been six months since Clare Ferguson, former army helicopter pilot and current Episcopal priest, and Russ Van Alstyne, police chief of Miller's Kill worked together on their first crime. They've been studiously avoiding one another ever since in an effort to keep their mutual attraction from gaining ground. During the Fourth of July holiday, two gay men are attacked and badly beaten in a manner that appears to be a hate crime. Clare is convinced Russ should warn the gay members of the town</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12415484227144343717">It's been six months since Clare Ferguson, former army helicopter pilot and current Episcopal priest, and Russ Van Alstyne, police chief of Miller's Kill worked together on their first crime. They've been studiously avoiding one another ever since in an effort to keep their mutual attraction from gaining ground. During the Fourth of July holiday, two gay men are attacked and badly beaten in a manner that appears to be a hate crime. Clare is convinced Russ should warn the gay members of the town but Russ isn't convinced it's a specific hate crime. When the third attack kills a developer involved in a high profile land development deal, Russ suspects there may be more to these attacks than anti-gay grievances. Many people in town are involved in the protests against the land development deal since contaminated PCB ponds have been found in the area. Economic supporters want the jobs and the environmentalist want to stop the development.<br /><br />Maybe I should be uncomfortable with the growing attraction between Russ and Clare but I'm not. Russ is happily married to a woman who we never hear from in the books and is kept “off stage” in a clever move. They both want to be friends but that is so difficult when they are such soul mates, to use a corny phrase. They use a lot of humorous dialog and their characters are so different and interesting. The character development is never done at the expense of a well plotted mystery. The small town of Miller's Kill will be familiar to any reader who ever lived in one. The author has a good eye for detail and there's a fabulously exciting, well-written helicopter scene in this story. <br /><br />If you are worried about reading a preachy type story rest assured these are not religiously themed mysteries. While Clare is an Episcopal priest the books don't focus on religion. The prayers and Episcopalian rituals are added for atmosphere and I find them completely unobtrusive. Great series of mysteries. I'm already on book three and have picked up the others, as well. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12415484227144343717">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3879748785261143436">Another good entry in this series, although for me not quite as good as the first.<br />Gay men are being viciously attacked in this story and the Chief, with good reason, doesn't want to believe the attacks are hate crimes.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText3879748785261143436">Another good entry in this series, although for me not quite as good as the first.<br />Gay men are being viciously attacked in this story and the Chief, with good reason, doesn't want to believe the attacks are hate crimes. Additionally, a group of townspeople are protesting a new construction project that may be forcing PCBs into the water supply.<br />I felt like there were too many disparate story lines here, though I will admit that they were all finally tied together. Also, Clare's involvement in the investigation was a bit too much to believe. <br />I still really enjoy the main characters and the tension between them. Interesting (and good) to see Clare dating. Loved meeting Russ' mother, I hope she shows up in future installments. I also liked how the author brought in current issues. Looking forward to reading more in this series. </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12525934669549576656">The Priest and the Chief are at it again: circling around each other, trying to ignore that their feelings that go deeper than friendship, and also trying to solve a murder.<br /><br />Clare is the one who stumbles on the exsanguinated body during the 4th of July fireworks, alerted by the dogs she is taking care of while their owner is in the hospital, victim of an apparent gay-bashing incident.<br /><br />The murder victim is also a gay man, and his death is apparently one more step in the anti-homosexual violence plaguing Millers Kill. Or is it?<br /><br />Clare is still learning how to fit into the community. Her liberal stances and social activism aren't sitting extremely well with the St. Albans Vestry. They are still mad about the press she got the previous winter and now she's out in front of the media talking about homosexuality. Oy gevalt.<br /><br />Clare and Russ seem like such nice people...people I would like to know. But the way everyone in Millers Kill is up in everyone's business would drive me crazy. <br /><br />I also have a question: when in this series will I get to see/meet Mrs. Van Alstyne, the younger?</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sdosHlcAOK7IbkTR1VHduHuA/OnoDGVa3cYUtM7rubvUDhPNpdIsVES2MGqrMDsKMnc/8KHRIvC3zxEmAn5P/g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JFYuQLJ9MF2x3krTGjRhhOS1pog1PJpI0u0t7BcwBDpBghGTQK8kpz0GPmhkVYc2rUJlkXzh3eK45Ch+26Xyfw==')})
  }

Emotions explode in the novel Julia Spencer-Fleming\'s readers have been clamoring for. Police Chief Russ Van Alstyne\'s first encounter with Clare Fergusson was in the hospital emergency room on a freezing December night. A newborn infant had been abandoned on the town\'s Episcopal church steps. If Russ had known that the church had a new priest, he certainly would never have guessed that it would be a woman. Not a woman like Clare. That night in the hospital was the beginning of an attraction so fierce, so forbidden, that the only thing that could keep them safe from compromising their every belief was distance---but in a small town like Millers Kill, distance is hard to find.\n\nRuss Van Alstyne figures his wife kicking him out of their house is nobody\'s business but his own. Until a neighbor pays a friendly visit to Linda Van Alstyne ­and finds the woman\'s body, gruesomely butchered, on the kitchen floor. To the state police, it\'s an open-and-shut case of a disaffected husband, silencing first his wife, then the murder investigation he controls. To the townspeople, it\'s proof that the whispered gossip about the police chief and the priest was true. To the powers-that-be in the church hierarchy, it\'s a chance to control their wayward cleric once and for all. Obsession. Lies. Nothing is as it seems in Millers Kill, where betrayal twists old friendships and evil waits inside quaint white clapboard farmhouses.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"1447583130066065816\"
